id="top"></a>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-featured-star" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_lists" title="This is a featured list. Click here for more information."><img alt="This is a featured list. Click here for more information." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/20px-Cscr-featured.svg.png" width="20" height="19" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n\t\t\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Category 4 Pacific hurricanes</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A well developed hurricane approaching Baja California, Mexico, from the south. It features a mostly circular cloud mass surrounding a defined eye." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg/220px-Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg/330px-Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg/440px-Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6800" data-file-height="8800" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odile_Sept_14_2014_1755Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Odile" title="Hurricane Odile">Hurricane Odile</a> near its peak intensity. Odile had the lowest <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a> of a Category&#160;4 hurricane in the Pacific basins at 918&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 27.11&#160;<a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inHg</a>).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Category&#160;4, the second-highest classification on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[nb 1]</a></sup> is used for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> that have winds of 130\xe2\x80\x93156&#160;mph (209\xe2\x80\x93251&#160;km/h; 113\xe2\x80\x93136&#160;<a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">kn</a>). The division of the eastern and central Pacific basins occurs at 140\xc2\xb0&#160;W; the eastern Pacific covers area east of 140\xc2\xb0&#160;W, while the central Pacific extends between 140\xc2\xb0&#160;W to 180\xc2\xb0&#160;W. Both basins\' division points are at 66\xc2\xb0&#160;N as a northern point and the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> as the southern point. As of 2017, 118&#160;hurricanes have attained Category 4 status in the northeastern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> basins. This list does not include storms that also attained Category&#160;5 status on the scale.</p>\n<p>Numerous climatological factors influence the formation of hurricanes in the Pacific basins. The <a href="/wiki/North_Pacific_High" title="North Pacific High">North Pacific High</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Low" title="Aleutian Low">Aleutian Low</a>, usually present between January and April, cause strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and unfavorable conditions for the development of hurricanes. During its presence, <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o-Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a> results in increased numbers of powerful hurricanes through weaker wind shear, while <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Ni\xc3\xb1a">La Ni\xc3\xb1a</a> reduces the number of such hurricanes through the opposite. <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> may also influence the formation of tropical cyclones in the Pacific basin. During a thirty-year period with two sub-periods, the first between 1975 and 1989 and the second between 1990 and 2004, an increase of thirteen&#160;Category&#160;4 or 5 storms was observed from the first sub-period.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Statistics_and_background"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics and background</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Climatology"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Climatology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Category.C2.A04_Pacific_hurricanes"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Category&#160;4 Pacific hurricanes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Landfalls"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Landfalls</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_and_background">Statistics and background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Category_4_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Statistics and background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png" class="image"><img alt="Tracks of all known Category 4 Pacific hurricanes from 1949-2011 in the central and eastern Pacific basins." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png/260px-Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png" width="260" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png/390px-Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png/520px-Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Pacific_Category_4_hurricanes.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTracks of all known Category&#160;4 Pacific hurricanes from 1949-2011 in the central and eastern Pacific basins</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div style="padding-left:10px;padding-bottom:10px;">\n<table align="right" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="background:transparent;text-align:center">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="7" nowrap="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale</a></small></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#5ebaff;width:1.8em" title="Tropical Depression: &lt;39 mph (0\xe2\x80\x9362 km/h)">TD</td>\n<td style="background-color:#00faf4;width:1.8em" title="Tropical Storm: 39\xe2\x80\x9373 mph (63\xe2\x80\x93117 km/h)">TS</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ffffcc;width:1.8em" title="Category 1: 74\xe2\x80\x9395 mph (118\xe2\x80\x93153 km/h)">C1</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ffe775;width:1.8em" title="Category 2: 96\xe2\x80\x93110 mph (154\xe2\x80\x93177 km/h)">C2</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ffc140;width:1.8em" title="Category 3: 111\xe2\x80\x93130 mph (178\xe2\x80\x93209 km/h)">C3</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ff8f20;width:1.8em" title="Category 4: 131\xe2\x80\x93155 mph (210\xe2\x80\x93249 km/h)">C4</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ff6060;width:1.8em" title="Category 5: \xe2\x89\xa5156 mph (\xe2\x89\xa5250 km/h)">C5</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>, "Category&#160;4" is the second-most powerful classification, with winds ranging between 130\xe2\x80\x93156&#160;mph (209\xe2\x80\x93251&#160;km/h; 113\xe2\x80\x93136&#160;kn). When these hurricanes make <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a>, impacts are usually severe but are not as destructive as <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_5" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category&#160;5</a> hurricanes that come ashore.<sup id="cite_ref-sshws_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sshws-1">[1]</a></sup> The term "<a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained wind</a>" refers to the average wind speed measured during the period of one minute at the height of 10 feet (3.0&#160;m) above the ground. The windspeed is measured at that height to prevent disruption from obstructions. Wind gusts in tropical cyclones are usually approximately 30% stronger than the one-minute maximum sustained winds.<sup id="cite_ref-sustained_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sustained-3">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The northeastern Pacific hurricane basins are divided into two parts&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 eastern and central. The eastern Pacific basin extends from all areas of the Pacific north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> east of 140\xc2\xb0&#160;W, while the central Pacific basin includes areas north of the equator between 140\xc2\xb0&#160;W and 180\xc2\xb0&#160;W.<sup id="cite_ref-products-nws_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-products-nws-4">[3]</a></sup> Both basins extend to the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a> at 66\xc2\xb0&#160;N.<sup id="cite_ref-Longshore-Pacific_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longshore-Pacific-5">[4]</a></sup> When tropical cyclones cross from the Atlantic into the Pacific, the name of the previous storm is retained if the system continues to exhibit tropical characteristics; however, when hurricanes degenerate into a remnant <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a>, the system is designated with the next name on the rotating eastern Pacific hurricane naming list.<sup id="cite_ref-basin-1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basin-1-6">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Since 1900, 118&#160;Category&#160;4 hurricanes have been recorded in the eastern and central Pacific basins. Of these, thirteen have attained Category&#160;4 status on more than one occasion, by weakening to a status on the Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale lower than Category&#160;4 and later restrengthening into a Category&#160;4. Such storms are demarcated by the dates they first attained and the final time they lost the intensity. Only two storms, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fico_(1978)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Fico (1978)">Hurricane Fico</a> in 1978 and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Norbert_(1984)" title="Hurricane Norbert (1984)">Hurricane Norbert</a> in 1984, reached Category&#160;4 status three times or more.<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Between 1970 and 1975, advisories for systems in the eastern Pacific basins were initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Eastern Pacific Hurricane Center">Eastern Pacific Hurricane Center (EPHC)</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service (NWS)</a> office in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco, California</a>. At that time, the advisories released were written in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> Fleet Weather Center in <a href="/wiki/Alameda,_California" title="Alameda, California">Alameda</a> and the Air Force Hurricane Liaison Officer at the <a href="/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base" title="McClellan Air Force Base">McClellan Air Force Base</a>. Following the move of the hurricane center to <a href="/wiki/Redwood_City,_California" title="Redwood City, California">Redwood City</a> in 1976, track files were created and altered by Arthur Pike and were later re-modified following the release of a study in 1980. The <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center (NHC)</a> extended its authority to the EPHC in 1988, and subsequently began maintaining the tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-Blake-p.6_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blake-p.6-8">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climatology">Climatology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Category_4_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Climatology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandra_2015_track.png" class="image"><img alt="The track of Hurricane Kenneth in 2011" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/230px-Sandra_2015_track.png" width="230" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/345px-Sandra_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/460px-Sandra_2015_track.png 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1669" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandra_2015_track.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe track of <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Sandra" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">Hurricane Sandra</a> in 2015, which is the latest-forming Category&#160;4 hurricane on record in the northeastern Pacific basin.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>A total of 118&#160;Category&#160;4 hurricanes have been recorded in the eastern and central Pacific basins since 1900. Only two Category&#160;4 hurricanes have been recorded in May, in addition to 12&#160;in June, 22&#160;in July, 29&#160;in August, 32&#160;in September, 18&#160;in October, and two in November.<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup> No Category&#160;4 storms have developed during the off-season.<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup> It is theorized that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> was responsible for an increase of 13&#160;Category&#160;4 and 5 storms that developed in the eastern Pacific, from 36&#160;in the period of 1975\xe2\x80\x931989 to 49&#160;in the period of 1990\xe2\x80\x932004. It was estimated that if sea-surface temperatures ascended by 2 to 2.5&#160;degrees, the intensity of tropical cyclones would increase by 6\xe2\x80\x9310% internationally. During years with the existence of an <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o-Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a>, sea-surface temperatures increase in the eastern Pacific, resulting in an increase in activity as vertical wind shear decreases in the Pacific; the opposite happens in the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins#Northern_Atlantic_Ocean" title="Tropical cyclone basins">Atlantic basin</a> during El Ni\xc3\xb1o, when wind shear increases creating an unfavourable environment for tropical cyclone formation in the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-eo_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eo-9">[8]</a></sup> Contrary to El Ni\xc3\xb1o, <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Ni\xc3\xb1a">La Ni\xc3\xb1a</a> increases wind shear over the eastern Pacific and reduces it over the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-Longshore-El-Ni.C3.B1o_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longshore-El-Ni.C3.B1o-10">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The presence of a semi-permanent <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">high-pressure area</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/North_Pacific_High" title="North Pacific High">North Pacific High</a> in the eastern Pacific is a dominant factor against formation of tropical cyclones in the winter, as the Pacific High results in <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> that causes environmental conditions for tropical cyclone formation to be unconducive. Its effects in the central Pacific basin are usually related to keeping cyclones away from the Hawaiian Islands. Due to westward <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade wind">trade winds</a>, hurricanes in the Pacific nearly never head eastward, although several storms have defied the odds and headed eastward. A second factor preventing tropical cyclones from forming during the winter is the occupation of a semi-permanent <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a> designated the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Low" title="Aleutian Low">Aleutian Low</a> between January and April. Its presence over western Canada and the northwestern United States contributes to the area\'s occurrences of precipitation in that duration. In addition, its effects in the central Pacific near 160\xc2\xb0&#160;W causes tropical waves that form in the area to drift northward into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Alaska" title="Gulf of Alaska">Gulf of Alaska</a> and dissipate. Its retreat in late-April allows the warmth of the Pacific High to meander in, bringing its powerful clockwise wind circulation with it. The <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> departs southward in mid-May permitting the formation of the earliest <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical waves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Longshore-Pacific_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longshore-Pacific-5">[4]</a></sup> coinciding with the start of the eastern Pacific hurricane season on May&#160;15.<sup id="cite_ref-season_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-11">[10]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Cooler waters near the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> are thought to prevent storms in the eastern&#160;Pacific from transitioning into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a>; only three storms listed in the database are known to have successfully completed an extratropical transition.<sup id="cite_ref-Blake-p.6_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blake-p.6-8">[7]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (May 2016)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Talk:List_of_Category_4_Pacific_hurricanes#Dubious" title="Talk:List of Category 4 Pacific hurricanes">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span id="Category&#160;4_Pacific_hurricanes"></span><span class="mw-headline" colspan="7" align="center">\n<p><span style="font-size:95%">Notes:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%"><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /> The storm noted formed or attained Category&#160;4 status in the central Pacific basin but may have formed in the eastern Pacific basin</span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%"><img alt="double-dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /> The storm noted attained Category&#160;4 status more than once</span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%">* The storm noted was both a Category&#160;4 in the eastern and central Pacific basins</span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%">** The storm noted originated in the Atlantic basin, but later intensified into a Category&#160;4 hurricane in the eastern Pacific basin</span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%"># Storms that attained Category&#160;4 status at one point but intensified into Category&#160;5 at a later time are not included.</span></li>\n<li><span style="font-size:95%">As the Pacific hurricane database only goes back to 1949, the <a href="/wiki/1943_Mazatl%C3%A1n_hurricane" title="1943 Mazatl\xc3\xa1n hurricane">1943 Mazatl\xc3\xa1n hurricane</a> is not included, although it attained Category&#160;4-equivalent winds at 136&#160;mph (219&#160;km/h). It is unknown if the winds observed were sustained.<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mwr-1943_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-1943-85">[84]</a></sup></span></li>\n</ul>\n<ul>\n<li>Storms that formed in the eastern or central Pacific but strengthened to reach Category&#160;4 status in the western Pacific basin (west of 180\xc2\xb0&#160;W) are not included.<sup id="cite_ref-WPac-basin_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPac-basin-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Atlantic-HURDAT_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlantic-HURDAT-87">[86]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landfalls">Landfalls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Category_4_Pacific_hurricanes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Landfalls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table style="border-style:solid; border-width:1px; border-color:#c0c0c0; background-color:#fdfdfd; text-align:left; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;" cellpadding="1">\n<caption style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">Landfalls</a> by month<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Month</th>\n<th scope="col" style="width: 15em};">Number of storms</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">June</th>\n<td>\n<div style="height: 1.25em; width: 15em;">\n<div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:1em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div>\n<span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 15em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">1</span></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">August</th>\n<td>\n<div style="height: 1.25em; width: 15em;">\n<div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:2em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div>\n<span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 15em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">2</span></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">September<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[nb 2]</a></sup></th>\n<td>\n<div style="height: 1.25em; width: 15em;">\n<div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:9em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div>\n<span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 15em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">9</span></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">October</th>\n<td>\n<div style="height: 1.25em; width: 15em;">\n<div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:13em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div>\n<span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 15em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">13</span></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Of the 118&#160;Category&#160;4 hurricanes that have formed in the eastern and central Pacific basins, 25&#160;have made <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a>. Of them, four made landfall at Category&#160;4 intensity, three at Category&#160;3, eleven at Categories&#160;2 and 1, six as tropical storms, and five as tropical depressions. Several of these storms weakened slightly after attaining Category&#160;4 status as they approached land;<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mwr-1943_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-1943-85">[84]</a></sup> this is usually a result of dry air, shallower water due to <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">shelving</a>, cooler waters, or interaction with land.<sup id="cite_ref-Katrina-TCR_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Katrina-TCR-89">[87]</a></sup> Only in five years&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1976, 1983, 1992, 1997, and 2014&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 more than one Category&#160;4 hurricane made landfall, and only during one year&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 1992&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 did three Category&#160;4 hurricanes made landfall.<sup id="cite_ref-hurdat_7-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurdat-7">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders sortable">\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Name</th>\n<th class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>, devised in 1971, is used to categorize the intensity of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclones" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical cyclones">tropical cyclones</a> in the Atlantic and Pacific Oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-sshws_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sshws-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Though <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juliette_(2001)" title="Hurricane Juliette (2001)">Hurricane Juliette</a> of 2001 made a second landfall in October, it did so after it re-generated. The landfall is included in the "September" total but not the "October" total.</span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</div>\n<dl>\n<dt>General</dt>\n</dl>\n<ul>\n<li><span id="Blake2009"></span><cite class="citation book">Blake, Eric S.; Gibney, Ethan J.; Brown, Daniel P.; Mainelli, Michelle M.; <a href="/wiki/James_Franklin_(meteorologist)" title="James Franklin (meteorologist)">Franklin, James L.</a>; Kimberlain, Todd B.; Hammer, Gregory R.
